Correct:
- a â†’ 14 is smaller than 15, boolean expression evaluates to `True`
- e â†’ 14 is bigger than 12, boolean expression evaluates to `True`
Incorrect:
- b â†’ first `if` statement in line 3 already evaluated to `True`, `elif` is not checked
- c â†’ first `if` statement in line 3 already evaluated to `True`, `elif` is not checked
- d â†’ `if` statement in line 11 evaluated to `True`, `else` is not checked
- f â†’ `if` statement in line 11 evaluated to `True`, `else` is not checked

Modulo returns us the rest of a division.
1. Check for next number dividable by 13 without rest â€”> 13
1. Calculate difference between 17 and 13 â€”> 17 - 13 = **4**

Division always returns float datatype

```python
type(4/2)
<class 'float'>
```

- Multiplication with `float` values is possible
- No, Python just executes whatever you give, if you provide for example `Strings` instead of `Integers`, Python will still try to do the calculation but then throws an error
- Yes, we have three `Integer` values. Thus, multiplication is possible

In line 3 we override variable b with letters `"ba"` , the number of equation marks does not matter.

- 15 is a normal `Integer` value and is stored in `x`
- `x (15) / 2` equals `7.5`, which is a `float` value and is stored in `y`
- `str(x)` converts the Integer value 15 to String `"15"` with `+` we concetate two strings, thus `z` is equal to `â€œ1515â€` and thus a `str`

- In the first iteration, the while loop is executed as 4 is bigger than 3, thus â€œGreenâ€ is printed. In line 5, `x` is reduced by 1 and now equal to 3. We jump back to line 3 and check if `x` is still bigger than 3. However, as this is no longer the case (`x` is equal to 3), we skip the while loop and jump to line 6.
- After the while loop is terminated, â€œWhiteâ€ is printed
- `print(â€whiteâ€)` is not part of the while loop which can be inferred from the indentation and thus is only executed once the while loop has been terminated
- Green is only printed once
- The while-loop terminates after the first iteration as `x` is equal to 3 and no longer bigger than 3
- The condition of the while loop evaluates to True in the first iteration
- Green is printed in the first iteration of the while loop

No, this is not possible, we can only do mathematical operations with two values of the same data type. If we try to do so, we receive an error:
```python
2 + '5'
TypeError: unsupported operand type(s) for +: 'int' and 'str'
```


ðŸ“„ **[Quiz 2]** (subpage)

- 5 is the first number to be included
- 14 the first number to be excluded
- 1 is the step size â€”> we donâ€™t over-jump any number
```python
liste = list(range(5,14,1))
print(liste)
[5, 6, 7, 8, 9, 10, 11, 12, 13]
len(liste) 
9
```
â€”> The range object consists of 9 elements, thus the loop is executed 9 times

Of course, we can have nested while loops.

---

![image](https://prod-files-secure.s3.us-west-2.amazonaws.com/85904fa9-813f-4181-815c-7a9adaee3156/28281cbd-69cf-4e6c-8635-690cfa17f68f/Untitled.png?X-Amz-Algorithm=AWS4-HMAC-SHA256&X-Amz-Content-Sha256=UNSIGNED-PAYLOAD&X-Amz-Credential=ASIAZI2LB4662YJ5KR3H%2F20251214%2Fus-west-2%2Fs3%2Faws4_request&X-Amz-Date=20251214T005050Z&X-Amz-Expires=3600&X-Amz-Security-Token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEF8aCXVzLXdlc3QtMiJIMEYCIQCjKkUEl7qzEZbApB9%2Bj6zybv8LTJrZpKReUBcdsGjvqgIhALZDZ%2BNAba9ZDx%2Fo5KnT5DZIvyO6XykdzsmIDg%2FUolV%2FKv8DCCcQABoMNjM3NDIzMTgzODA1IgwE5%2FutvXR09CA1%2F4Uq3APxdl2r16mPPiiV3d6cTaXKWnc51%2FkEusjI1XbL8x9aKboim8MFATRTTSez17OoQEuJsUGa2dfx7KhCfFtstueC1JmcBBMkX3sx2STCErXFj82Aw6IWf4RkfEIjz082e311bjZcWsTDRm%2BG09QT%2BcpdUBaVE8wny0BmEF5l%2BITz%2BNk%2F9p3%2FRqOmh7V%2BBieTvc81tsNFRNg9RZI5z7GgEtBE8sf%2FEpt942Svx6Z8QDt59%2B2F7d8Cz786PQoSu7OlM9IYLCEuGU2nuexZC5u6VSMx0S6S24GxGQf6nnM3dQx4FKz5IoESdDsxJPva%2F1LdObvHPGrOaPs3iTxl0ViBosnKiX7pQOa0zDWfaLnQIuN8n4JJm7C%2Bf8xeb05aj%2FvSMftieqc3RzNkDdGYZc3uvWYSSN1Ymwjtoq50Ga%2BHOGfrGRR6y5sRwXcA7N3NGg%2B7bXKgcf758iqDxqE5LegrC1jlebHdJXEDqQ314rJR9goFjL5kUFUhJzXGqS6S%2FXZReHrXR0eiDgHFQQsJoOzhIn9Cu3UDn%2F7jzDLlP4symg04vZvuQTquFN4z2ro4%2FiEiNuKbJrbg8nnAL2V1hVu791cVQ98dF%2BLD%2FgMIyKV6GmLLg4f9%2Fgve3OpXpGnY4TCEzvfJBjqkAXJag3XmWXzI%2B6ay57y3LkMD4fCosTY3lIFt%2FTgC8tOCkH%2BUR9pBrBjU3KrDJcLPZnceZAnVNw52mu33pBhuj%2BWWK9X8phTkwLMpThtP3OtUOeCXOnggKpSDIZeBl2XzLgSQLQhjUlc7sVhJX7gHE3YVPMHjvaFnIOUWvAn6Qs4x5JxS2pmBQiqPQfjMdIZvKxxK9eX9AzwpU3%2FfAd%2B8gYT10Ol7&X-Amz-Signature=68461a72e857c733e18eabe23e1da406014f16e45d6c08cdd38a544a543c11db&X-Amz-SignedHeaders=host&x-amz-checksum-mode=ENABLED&x-id=GetObject)
How does our range object look like? `[0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, â€¦ , 999]`
- First execution of for-loop
- `value = 0`
- `0 % 2` â€”> `0` â€”> `0 == 0` â€”> True â€”> line 5 is executed
- `â€˜0â€™` is added to `values` 
- Second execution of for-loop
- `value = 1`
- `1 % 2` â€”> `1 `â€”>  `1 == 0` â€”> False â€”> line 5 is not executed
- Third execution of for-loop:
- `value = 2`
- `2 % 2` â€”> `0` â€”> `0 == 0` â€”> True â€”> line 5 is executed
- `â€˜2â€™` is added to `values` 
etc.
In the end, all even numbers are stored in `values`. Since 998 is the last even number in the range object, this is also the last element in the string `values`.

How does our range object look like? `[11, 12, 13, 14, 15, 16, 17, 18, 19]`
- In line 4 we convert the value stored in `s` to a string and update the string `s`

- Correct, because we convert the variable `var` to a String which allows us to iterate over the string and store each element / number in the variable `num`, however as we want to calculate a sum, we need to convert the number back to an integer, which we do correctly in line 6 using `int(num)`
- Incorrect, because with every execution of the for-loop we override the variable `ds`, thus `ds` is always equal to `int(num)`, since we do not save the temporary result anywhere
- Incorrect, it is not possible to iterate through an Integer value, we must convert he integer to a string first using `str(var)`
```python
for i in 123:
	print("hello") 

TypeError: 'int' object is not iterable
```

ðŸ“„ **[Quiz 3]** (subpage)

Letâ€™s assume `elements = [3, 4, 5]`
Thus, `reversed(elements) = [5, 4, 3]`
- First run
- `value = 5`
- `5 % 2` â€”> 1 â€”>` 1 â‰  0 `â€”> True
- `to_return = 5`
- Second run
- `value = 4`
- `4 % 2` â€”> 0 â€”> `0 â‰  0` â€”> False
- line 5 not executed
- Third run
- `value = 3`
- `3 % 2 `â€”> 1 â€”> `1 â‰  0` â€”> True
- `to_return = 3`
**â€”> 3 was the first odd value in list ****`elements`**

---

| Line | a | b | c |

| 1 | `[1, 2, 3, 4.0, 5]` | - | - |

- b is a float

How does our range object look like? `start` is the first number to be included, `end` is the first number to be excluded
- Correct, end is the first number to be excluded in line 4 we update the value of `result` by adding the value stored in `i`
- Incorrect, when I only provide one parameter value, then it will be used as `start` as this is the first positional parameter of the function and `end` will be assigned the default value 10, thus my range object would only contain the number 9 and thus the function would return the `result` value 9 
- Correct, if end value of range object is smaller than start value, the range object is empty. Thus, we never execute the for-loop and never update the `result` variable which is why its initial value (0) is returned
- Incorrect, `end` is the first value that is excluded from the range object
- Incorrect, `range(1, 1)` leads to `[ ]`, and thus for-loop is never executed and result variable not update, however, no error is thrown
- Incorrect, I have default parameters specified (`start = 1`, `end = 10`). Thus, when no parameters are provided then the values 1 and 10 are used, when only one parameter is provided, then this value is assigned to `start` and 10 is used for `end`
- Correct, `0 + 1 + 2 + 3 = 6`
- Incorrect, the function is defined correctly, i.e., no syntax error is present
- Correct, it does not matter how the variables are called that you are passing to the function, the function uses anyway its own temporary variables, `start` and `end`

- True, because we donâ€™t change the items inside the two tuples, we only hang them together
Remember: Updating an item inside a tuple, e.g., replacing `1` in `tpl_1` with `3` is not possible!

- For `start` and `end` we have default values defined â€”> **not mandatory **to pass these parameters to function
- For `text` we have no default value defined â€”> **mandatory** to pass this parameter to function

ðŸ“„ **[Quiz 4]** (subpage)
![image](https://prod-files-secure.s3.us-west-2.amazonaws.com/85904fa9-813f-4181-815c-7a9adaee3156/efc1be34-8141-46fb-bce2-7407370f6b2e/Untitled.png?X-Amz-Algorithm=AWS4-HMAC-SHA256&X-Amz-Content-Sha256=UNSIGNED-PAYLOAD&X-Amz-Credential=ASIAZI2LB466432AAMJ6%2F20251214%2Fus-west-2%2Fs3%2Faws4_request&X-Amz-Date=20251214T005059Z&X-Amz-Expires=3600&X-Amz-Security-Token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEF8aCXVzLXdlc3QtMiJGMEQCICLnWADcc0Ex9TPInqJxGfvme9PQVYBc2LWhNz8c61ynAiB89oaKnJjvlnK8GT%2FoOpfvz6uLPNPx2uFHA7rR7ncgQCr%2FAwgnEAAaDDYzNzQyMzE4MzgwNSIM3u6NzQhI4706lMjQKtwD6VCrPJaj2KDnvXDVTcV0s1tvsVx35DjbsCt7gw3CHkpFxuM6eu3RJKxZgXTVKvl%2BcPVGygi1KUfq6jdat1j4VpV6i%2FJAknqUh1a1VZnuwEXVbzGwP4WRd6PZAaKLYCcwo2w2mA95Emozxky9TtPPVjV0pfHWSZXdcmhmMqGF5rFR6ga48OGf7jmqLwcmOsz%2FEdDTiTSo2%2Be8cm%2FGZ6lvqDQBlxbDv7UwIDz%2BkLyc2ZNe8L4p%2Fc7O3ITYlcAP1rs432%2FGyGU2qelTXRGJVJkcBM2UGtVyKZcPwkGBEwT%2B3eQhdF1ahY4QDuasRBW%2B7H4nDYmVf6XvoLB%2B41jPKFLhggjdO8Wf3DsADedjET%2BI%2BPcHp3CTxxxoVlSkg2grtzzbIclx1MEtCTi3wzMUAZZ5EHHUj%2FBVH1FbFkGSZHAd7dplIsSHjTCj6C0lvoke6hA0dJAYSHPzcALce%2BezqKiszG6WXkYdc3yPNTZ44zykJzRBxyIu7EP67%2Fz4rLPhxbCkjOYDHKcreNlpdKAmflModl4eCRDbFwbEO8uGM9lsdBjm4BLhYIwkeHVkIbLlZyDFh%2BXVPLII8T92Yvij%2BrHaeTDbVNqOnFsKqrWp%2FE0c6LumlYospEbkkIUnfOwwyM73yQY6pgERc7OpQR8tqnm41wPyTHDrTVjjmjJcsrafSzx3nlyfnDK3brJYyusmjoa40cbT6yuwBS4wGw2U0tWtoVXeNph6HaZoNTQ6MwfMCG6YakdmDrmu%2BTYknBgwzupQTK5lbKuHNQVa0VqEM2AUTLCrJUqZuHW1oUGgmgVtChvCY1aCjw9%2F8jsJiKGjg2Rb7yNE8d4Z1vo4wGBgrhjjplHLkykVCAKTnrfF&X-Amz-Signature=f81f75136bbc0939b2cbb8e6f7f6436d34098eea5472f50f2cf120fc5d7d0e7a&X-Amz-SignedHeaders=host&x-amz-checksum-mode=ENABLED&x-id=GetObject)

- First we execute `map(f, range(6)) `
- We pass each element in `[0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5]` into the function `def f(x)`
- Function def f(x) is executed 6 times
- As a result we get `[0, 2, 4, 6, 8, 10]`
- Now we execute `map(f, [0, 2, 4, 6, 8, 10])`
- We pass each element in` [0, 2, 4, 6, 8, 10] `into the function def `f(x)`
- Function def f(x) is executed 6 times
- As a result we get `[0, 4, 8, 12, 16, 20]`
How many times did we execute `def f(x)` ? â€”> **12 times**

---

- We take each element in `[0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6]` and assign it to `x`
- We multiply `x` by 2 
- Thus, each element is multiplied by 2 and result is `[0, 2, 4, 6, 8, 10, 12]`

![image](https://prod-files-secure.s3.us-west-2.amazonaws.com/85904fa9-813f-4181-815c-7a9adaee3156/7925737f-daac-41c5-a855-e605a07160b1/Untitled.png?X-Amz-Algorithm=AWS4-HMAC-SHA256&X-Amz-Content-Sha256=UNSIGNED-PAYLOAD&X-Amz-Credential=ASIAZI2LB466432AAMJ6%2F20251214%2Fus-west-2%2Fs3%2Faws4_request&X-Amz-Date=20251214T005059Z&X-Amz-Expires=3600&X-Amz-Security-Token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEF8aCXVzLXdlc3QtMiJGMEQCICLnWADcc0Ex9TPInqJxGfvme9PQVYBc2LWhNz8c61ynAiB89oaKnJjvlnK8GT%2FoOpfvz6uLPNPx2uFHA7rR7ncgQCr%2FAwgnEAAaDDYzNzQyMzE4MzgwNSIM3u6NzQhI4706lMjQKtwD6VCrPJaj2KDnvXDVTcV0s1tvsVx35DjbsCt7gw3CHkpFxuM6eu3RJKxZgXTVKvl%2BcPVGygi1KUfq6jdat1j4VpV6i%2FJAknqUh1a1VZnuwEXVbzGwP4WRd6PZAaKLYCcwo2w2mA95Emozxky9TtPPVjV0pfHWSZXdcmhmMqGF5rFR6ga48OGf7jmqLwcmOsz%2FEdDTiTSo2%2Be8cm%2FGZ6lvqDQBlxbDv7UwIDz%2BkLyc2ZNe8L4p%2Fc7O3ITYlcAP1rs432%2FGyGU2qelTXRGJVJkcBM2UGtVyKZcPwkGBEwT%2B3eQhdF1ahY4QDuasRBW%2B7H4nDYmVf6XvoLB%2B41jPKFLhggjdO8Wf3DsADedjET%2BI%2BPcHp3CTxxxoVlSkg2grtzzbIclx1MEtCTi3wzMUAZZ5EHHUj%2FBVH1FbFkGSZHAd7dplIsSHjTCj6C0lvoke6hA0dJAYSHPzcALce%2BezqKiszG6WXkYdc3yPNTZ44zykJzRBxyIu7EP67%2Fz4rLPhxbCkjOYDHKcreNlpdKAmflModl4eCRDbFwbEO8uGM9lsdBjm4BLhYIwkeHVkIbLlZyDFh%2BXVPLII8T92Yvij%2BrHaeTDbVNqOnFsKqrWp%2FE0c6LumlYospEbkkIUnfOwwyM73yQY6pgERc7OpQR8tqnm41wPyTHDrTVjjmjJcsrafSzx3nlyfnDK3brJYyusmjoa40cbT6yuwBS4wGw2U0tWtoVXeNph6HaZoNTQ6MwfMCG6YakdmDrmu%2BTYknBgwzupQTK5lbKuHNQVa0VqEM2AUTLCrJUqZuHW1oUGgmgVtChvCY1aCjw9%2F8jsJiKGjg2Rb7yNE8d4Z1vo4wGBgrhjjplHLkykVCAKTnrfF&X-Amz-Signature=5b2ee2b9b75bbb8b0366060987ff663298ed0ee3fc323075f30002fc82c1d86b&X-Amz-SignedHeaders=host&x-amz-checksum-mode=ENABLED&x-id=GetObject)

- Incorrect, the execution will break as we never meet the stop condition as we pass on a negative numbers as parameters fro the recursive execution
â†’ `fibonacci(0 - 2)` + `fibonacci(0 - 1)`
- Correct, we see this as in line 10 we call the same function from within this function
- Correct, we donâ€™t have a stop condition so when we pass another number into the function then the function will never terminate. If we execute it with `number = 1` then the if condition in line 7 is met and thus we go not into the else statement and consequently no recursive function call happens and we do not end up in an endless loop.

If you are not familiar how a [recursive fibonacci function](https://www.geeksforgeeks.org/python-program-for-program-for-fibonacci-numbers-2/) is executed, check below.
```python
# Function for nth Fibonacci number
def Fibonacci(n):
   
    # Check if input is 0 then it will
    # print incorrect input
    if n < 0:
        print("Incorrect input")
 
    # Check if n is 0
    # then it will return 0
    elif n == 0:
        return 0
 
    # Check if n is 1,2
    # it will return 1
    elif n == 1 or n == 2:
        return 1
 
    else:
        return Fibonacci(n-2) + Fibonacci(n-1)
 
# Driver Program
print(Fibonacci(5))
```
---
**`fibonacci(5)`** **â†’ ****5**
n = 5
- **`fibonacci(3)`** + **`fibonacci(4)`** â†’ 2 + 3 = 5
- **`fibonacci(3)`**** â†’ ****2**
- n = 3
- **`fibonacci(1)`** + **`fibonacci(2)`** â†’ 1 + 1 = 2
- **`fibonacci(1)`**** â†’ ****1**
- return **1**
- **`fibonacci(2)`**** â†’ ****1**
- **`fibonacci(0)`** + **`fibonacci(1)`** â†’ 0 + 1 = 1
- **`fibonacci(0)`**** â†’ ****0**
- n = 0
- return **0**
- **`fibonacci(1)`**** â†’ ****1**
- n = 1
- return **1**
- **`fibonacci(4)`**** â†’ ****3**
- n = 4
- **`fibonacci(2)`** + **`fibonacci(3)`** â†’ 1 + 2 = 3
- **`fibonacci(2)`** **â†’ ****1**
- n = 2
- **`fibonacci(0)`** + **`fibonacci(1)`** â†’ 0 + 1 = 1
- **`fibonacci(0)`**** â†’ ****0**
- n = 0
- return 0
- **`fibonacci(1)`**** â†’ ****1**
- n = 1
- return 1
- **`fibonacci(3)`**** â†’ ****2**
- n = 3
- **`fibonacci(1)`** + **`fibonacci(2)`** â†’ 1 + 1 = 2
- **`fibonacci(1)`**** â†’ ****1**
- n = 1
- return 1
- **`fibonacci(2)`**** â†’ ****1**
- n = 2
- **`fibonacci(0)`** + **`fibonacci(1)`** â†’ 0 + 1 = 1
- **`fibonacci(0)`** **â†’ ****0**
- n = 0
- return **0**
- **`fibonacci(1)`** **â†’ ****1**
- n = 1
- return 1

We want to remove any elements in the three sub-lists that are not string
What happens if we pass the first sub-list `[1, â€œHelloâ€, False]` into `get_strings()`?
- First run
- `element = 1`
- `type(element)` â†’ int â†’ `int == str `â†’ False
- Second run
- `element = â€œHelloâ€`
- `type(element)` â†’ str â†’ `str == str` â†’ True
- `return_value = [â€Helloâ€]`
- Third run
- `element = False`
- `type(element)` â†’ bool â†’ `bool == str` â†’ False
- `[â€Helloâ€]` is returned from function
Function successfully filters out any elements that are not Strings.
How can we apply a function on every element of an Iterable, i.e., on all three sub-lists? â†’ `map() `function â†’ **`result = list(map(get_string, mixed_lists))`**

- Correct, `lambda` is an anonymous function, the function does not have a name, unlike a usual `def some_function()`, thus we can not re-call the function
- Correct
- If we multiply an odd number by 2, i.e., 3 * 2 we get an even number as a result
- If we multiply an even number by 2, i.e., 4 * 2 we get an even number as a result
- Thus, the result list will only contain even numbers, no matter if `num` is even or odd
- Incorrect, the function has a name: `lambda` â†’ just a regular function named lambda, remember: we can name functions and variables however we want to
- Correct
- Frist, range(num) is executed â†’ e.g. range(3) â†’ [0, 1, 2]
- Second we iterate over range object
- First run
- `x = 0`
- `x % 2` â†’ 0 â†’ `0 == 0` â†’ True
- `list_of_even_numbers = [0]`
- Second run
- `x = 1`
- `x % 2` â†’ 1 â†’ `1 == 0` â†’ False
- Third run
- `x = 2`
- `2 % 2` â†’ 0 â†’ `0 == 0` â†’ True
- `list_of_even_numbers = [0, 2]`
- Odd number (1) has been filtered out and the result contains only odd numbers

- Can we even access the age attribute of the Person class? Yes, the attribute is private but we have a getter method implemented `@property`
- We set result to `persons[0]` â†’ how old is the first person? â†’ 17, thus initially `result = 17`
- We iterate over all elements in persons
- First run
- `person = persons[0]`
- `person.age = 17`
- `17 < 17` â†’ False
- Second run
- `person = persons[1]`
- `person.age = 13`
- `13 < 17` â†’ True
- `result = 13`
- Third run
- `person = persons[2]`
- `person.age = 13`
- `13 < 13` â†’ False
- Fourth run
- `person = persons[3]`
- `person.age = 20`
- `20 < 17` â†’ False
- Fifth run
- `person = persons[4]`
- `person.age = 15`
- `15 < 13` â†’ False
- Sixth run
- `person = persons[5]`
- `person.age = 20`
- `20< 13` â†’ False
- Value of `result`? â†’ 13

- Incorrect, it is possible to return multiple value from a function
- Correct, we save the new power levels of the two superheroes in two variables (line 2 & 3), however, these variables exist only within the function `def fight()`, when the function was executed, the new power levels are lost. Instead, we should overwrite the attributes of the two superheroes with the values stored in `self_powerlevel_new` and `enemy_powerlevel_new` inside the function `def fight()`
- Incorrect, we donâ€™t modify any attribute value of the two superheroes, thus we donâ€™t need setter methods at all
- Incorrect, `self.powerlevel` is still the old value as we did not update it so far, we only created a new local variable `self_powerlevel_new` that does only exist within the function `def fight()`

Correct, with `super().__init__()` we can execute the constructor of the parent class

Incorrect, it is best-practice to use getter and setter methods to access or modify private attributes. However, Python cannot enforce this. Thus, even when we have a private attribute and we access it with `object._age` from outside the class, this still works technically, but does not comply with best practices as we should define a getter (and setter) method with `@property` so we can access then the attribute with `object.age`

---

![image](https://prod-files-secure.s3.us-west-2.amazonaws.com/85904fa9-813f-4181-815c-7a9adaee3156/1421c060-7162-4f7b-9c9f-6aff6c119a06/Untitled.png?X-Amz-Algorithm=AWS4-HMAC-SHA256&X-Amz-Content-Sha256=UNSIGNED-PAYLOAD&X-Amz-Credential=ASIAZI2LB466Y5V7ENAZ%2F20251214%2Fus-west-2%2Fs3%2Faws4_request&X-Amz-Date=20251214T005116Z&X-Amz-Expires=3600&X-Amz-Security-Token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEF8aCXVzLXdlc3QtMiJGMEQCIHj70ulP0ZHZwJOKUbIODniMnXC3JX1YTeSgLi4drsC9AiBqYMogojU%2BkQ9U0XkZJHs0m2ycJgN10W%2BLCptNpuUPIir%2FAwgnEAAaDDYzNzQyMzE4MzgwNSIMH8o30v6D21BBYWiuKtwDFKQl22kDmUH5SUb2TPyRmhJ0O8M6AzRd3BlPgcUQ%2FA6AokjnuDWI2xq3DnT5cTBpUOZQHq4Bh2voTF0CzY9Jmajfbde2J6Ymf9mxr3wPnnU%2FuggxK2JNjW6ABWKH0uLn7TyyboxmfBh4LrUmTgSURPB0QvzAExkmyuSVg4korolIJrFJ%2B%2B%2FnMz0VgV8vsU93CnhZEM%2Bc%2BmO5jKqg8r3kIDe1Qdn6PhBa56%2BPkncX8VOk%2Fx%2FQhvC5mfuggfVE2rvFMRVqU3OEXyx7%2F%2FYIZGFiQwD%2BJc5HTnlK7d0Z5KB%2BNo33eNmDja6WkCIWxo3O7qWlEMvJBqyG4xv4EJwF73hBSqimBcczqsH1%2FaJV7VcleQodT3%2F4%2BtbaoRxJJfEVmFdy8EpFE4NSGdvNPC7P4NKAu%2FFYe%2BbZgKJECoMR9M%2B2p80PsJac1yLjY8MOQ6TXj5F6Y3rNWhV4NH1jLdC%2FbyrmTe8t13%2BahyynWee1OjiLsGv1vtPtYGW6Iy980rsDD3R6L7uqiImTeAJMBaIBS3xx4viy5W5MHM3w3%2F4mP64iv3cIbJqmVcOIrfJ4eXV2miHChHe8%2BphQV3cMy%2BiYcdWZbkOyHYI95f%2FB8z73DyBhTzmGfDArK8MUmhtNyCMw4M33yQY6pgE8GrsrszUj%2F8EjHxKlUjjqRMvcC8LUjNWP5yu97TwVeSmgzWcY9QjEq%2BO%2BEb33DtABHxhxLuucyfjqFEeMSsvSNvvwusEaROoXmUp9XoNC%2FaAOtVLezfKNkLf5cFAQLYZwZLXi%2Fy2g2JpmTK2mOiO9q1T9qFDiDScqkELLX%2FgqtFR4DvpQis6OuKXn4Tl52dU5%2FTkLDUIulN%2BAXiU4BCpJ%2B1Fg3tHD&X-Amz-Signature=4ae58f7c4ed646d2ef36d9e8c18ab343c3450051bc73014b2ffa19a6915db179&X-Amz-SignedHeaders=host&x-amz-checksum-mode=ENABLED&x-id=GetObject)

Correct, it would be good to define the name attribute on the level of the parent class, `Person`, as likely every person has a name, even those that are no superheroes and so we would avoid duplicate and redundancies

- **A:** Correct, syntax of map: `map(<< some function >>, << some iterable >>)`, then the map functions takes each element out of the iterable and throws it into the defined function, often this is a `lambda` function but we can also call regular functions that are defined as `def some_name()`, important is that map() always returns a map object, thus in order to interpret the output of map we wrap it into the list() function, so our fucntion becomes `list(map(<< some function >>, << some iterable >>))`
- **B:** Correct, syntax of filer: `filter(<< some function that returns a boolean value >>, << some iterable >>)`, the filter function takes as well each element out of the iterable and throws it into the function, that must return either `True` or `False`, all those elements for which the function returned `False` are removed from the output and all those element for which the function returned `True` are kept

In line 21 we create the following object
Hero:
streetname = â€œSupermanâ€
Person:
name = â€œClark Kentâ€
age = 48

- If we execute print(superman) the method `Hero.__str__()` is executed
- Inside `Hero.__str__()` we call `super().__str__()`
- Inside `Person.__str__()` we return the string `My name is Clark Kent`
- we take the return value from `Person.__str__()`, `My name is Clark Kent` and add `, also known as Superman` to it
- As a return value from `Hero.__str__()` we receive `My name is Clark Kent, also known as Superman`, thus this is the output that is printed to the console

- `__repr__()` is only called when we print the object variable without the return statement, e.g. when we type `superman` into the console and hit enter
- Answer three would be correct if we would not have manually implemented the method `__str__()`

- Correct, inside `find_connection()` we call the Open Transport API and inside `find_restaurants()` we call the Yelp API, thus we have two HTTP requests. In both cases we retrieve data from the servers, thus we have two HTTP GET requests.
- Incorrect, with `obscure` we perform a slicing operation on the restaurants list in line 11, we can not perform slicing with a string, this would lead to an error
```python
liste = [1,2,3,4]
liste[:"janick"]

TypeError: slice indices must be integers or None or have an __index__ method
```
- Correct, `obscure` is an integer, so that we can filter out the first x restaurants in line 11
- Incorrect, when we call the Yelp API we want to retrieve information about available restaurants and not modify any resource on the server, thus we use a GET and not a POST request

From line 1 we can see that we are looking for the resource `/connections` on the Transport Open Data server, thus we must look into the part of the API documentation that describes the `/connections` resource. The documentation is [here available](https://transport.opendata.ch/docs.html#connections).
Inside the documentation we see the following:
![image](https://prod-files-secure.s3.us-west-2.amazonaws.com/85904fa9-813f-4181-815c-7a9adaee3156/3fea5020-b75f-4770-b9e8-c8d3823ec567/Untitled.png?X-Amz-Algorithm=AWS4-HMAC-SHA256&X-Amz-Content-Sha256=UNSIGNED-PAYLOAD&X-Amz-Credential=ASIAZI2LB466YBCELIUR%2F20251214%2Fus-west-2%2Fs3%2Faws4_request&X-Amz-Date=20251214T005126Z&X-Amz-Expires=3600&X-Amz-Security-Token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEF8aCXVzLXdlc3QtMiJIMEYCIQCE9WUY7n%2Fj2ZzeTEWYqOB%2BhqHWgSMjmX56mE4taWBLEwIhAKnqVV3AMJcSg4oYd1kWmeFz75k35FdQfGUDGQFB9Ot5Kv8DCCcQABoMNjM3NDIzMTgzODA1IgxCJCNGW6q4RwG%2BYCcq3ANCrvxUe7MDz%2BzHDN78sOpBqWdd3uGCywWVLxsPsC1Mmix%2FfBDRpxcEcXM%2FaMhXfFMOCQS32MApoaN9LVIzhjMSPb6xREHuz9Yw0jodN4SWutSeN78dxE9x%2BrtM%2FtvHtVpZwX%2FKHUoQHr50kE1WdhenxUQngQQ7ECvawsa4BRwRmedyUxo3fbsGY8WiPoGU47fBDvvuGjWfYHd9FCjGR4XyO6qld6SAuQEOtjc3ybY8qB6jZpm8EToveBNXQKr2SKJpMCngJKrH%2B5YHUyDxlqdKqwVoJVHyBXcbEpUZ7T1WhP9MG%2FRgERT4CDTDy%2BdFGUkNulxnk%2F88HTWMKboaZAlSRNdaGuaF7V4uPYoe72pZxobiD%2BtHwYoI9xqFrPJg3rmIrQS9TsL8escA5gpV0z09g4PgXq7NreHGucetJ%2ByDyI4ZEMZ166awXcCjcaJQM8iqWsUEUgJPuBdzNoxqCnAX1pVemQ%2BQXEcuRXDICIudhcqKpKavvilFi5k67Zv0UktSwDLMEIzef00qZNcR2j6QMZDXdSXdr%2F5RdPWnDg9Kci0XSPp%2BZjjHINbS89wTesEaBHsr5uEwhCwJPmUQWiBvYykAAO2eMwh3irhYbPCyad6gZWCFZj4MvuCTsjD5zffJBjqkAU9sFuAHkbPNxXUmGBc4%2B3D840Xu1nR66Ykc7eiOsiwPsESJNOkVi%2B2u7S3ZsLLX6VxYHIyEuPmwjju7m8Z9cY9YFBeYXMCyrrT%2BRF%2FsXL9hqhRnOwwPip4Ou0FgF9wN5RLx3bIabLiDfQMp3R91Dk0uadCeSwWeU217q2wjPB0sNucLBPz4dBhpjCyyEalAyv0hvjp%2BUubu13u%2BVQQjEf%2Fh%2FJJK&X-Amz-Signature=7cb46500a54ff6732e139ad4d3e648e2cd889b920fdccb64756c50d23c1f0587&X-Amz-SignedHeaders=host&x-amz-checksum-mode=ENABLED&x-id=GetObject)
Thus, if we only want to have night trains, we must include `sleeper = 1` as parameter in our request.

- Correct, we want to retrieve data from the server and not modify any resource on the server, thus we must use the GET method. Also, in the [documentation](https://www.yelp.com/developers/documentation/v3/business_search) we see that this is a GET endpoint

- Correct, as mentioned before `/businesses/search` is a GET endpoint, thus when we send a POST request, as it is currently implemented, we receive an error message from the server
- Incorrect, we must always look at the [API documentation](https://www.yelp.com/developers/documentation/v3/business_search) to see what data types we must provide, it is true that all data is converted into JSON, which in fact is a string, however, the standardised structure of JSON strings allows to also include integers and all common data types
- Incorrect, we must send a GET request
- Correct, according to HTTP standard, API keys must be included in the header of a request
- Incorrect, the code is not working as our API key is not placed in the request header and we are using the wrong request method (POST instead of GET)

- Correct, both browsers send a request to the [unisg.ch](https://unisg.ch/) server
- Incorrect, local ports are application specific, they allow to distinguish between the connection of Chrome with [unisg.ch](http://unisg.ch/) server and Firefox with [unisg.ch](http://unisg.ch/) server
- True, each device has one IP address, we send both requests from the same device, thus they have the same IP address
- True, the remote server has one port over which requests come in, this is mostly 443 for https or 8080 for http, as can be inferred from the screenshot below, both browsers, Chrome & Safari have the same remote port (443)

- Incorrect, HTTP packets are encrypted with TLS / SSL
- Correct, HTTP packets were encrypted with TLS / SSL
- Incorrect, we can also send HTTP requests when we use UDP protocol, it is not mandatory to use TCP when exchanging data using the HTTP protocol

- `SELECT *` â†’ We want all columns
- `FROM students` â†’ the table is called Students
- `WHERE DATE(date_of_birth) = DATE (â€™2001-11-11â€™)` â†’ we want the person that was born on the 11.11.2001
- We convert the value stored in `date_of_birth` to a `DATE` object so that we can compare it with our string `â€˜2011-11-11â€™`, so that we are sure that we compare the same data types with each other as otherwise we would get an error

We want the average grade per course category. Thus, we must look into the different code snippets and check where we find `GORUP BY category`. â†’ **snippet 2**
All other code snippets are grouped based on another column and therefore not valid solutions. 
The query is executable in one SQL statements as we have three inner JOINs
- First, we join enrolments and grades to get the information to which enrolment a grade belongs to
```sql
SELECT *
FROM grades
INNER JOIN enrollments 
	ON enrollments.id = grades.enrollment_id
```

- Second, we join courses with enrolments so that we get the information about the course category as in the end we want to group the grades per category
```sql
SELECT *
FROM grades
INNER JOIN enrollments 
	ON enrollments.id = grades.enrollment_id
INNER JOIN courses 
	ON courses.id = enrollments.course_id
```

- Third, we join with students table to see by whom the grades were achieved
```sql
SELECT *
FROM grades
INNER JOIN enrollments 
	ON enrollments.id = grades.enrollment_id
INNER JOIN courses 
	ON courses.id = enrollments.course_id
INNER JOIN students 
  ON students.id = enrollments.student_id
```
![image](https://prod-files-secure.s3.us-west-2.amazonaws.com/85904fa9-813f-4181-815c-7a9adaee3156/91706ec3-cc77-42a8-a12b-69711347157f/Untitled.png?X-Amz-Algorithm=AWS4-HMAC-SHA256&X-Amz-Content-Sha256=UNSIGNED-PAYLOAD&X-Amz-Credential=ASIAZI2LB466XS5UBDHN%2F20251214%2Fus-west-2%2Fs3%2Faws4_request&X-Amz-Date=20251214T005130Z&X-Amz-Expires=3600&X-Amz-Security-Token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEF8aCXVzLXdlc3QtMiJHMEUCIHSVc2pQgzB0vzoLbvKbKlBurjSvUi%2FaKnFe2bd7SD7XAiEA1%2FjsFdJOXCteB%2FP2OBTwKAJ%2FaaAo4XT2mTZyzJvwCTEq%2FwMIJxAAGgw2Mzc0MjMxODM4MDUiDPRosKgAzWCqd7TLqSrcA6hweRVxOIrgIOwASQR7jz591wfGJWF21ZO5OD4ryG6ha66lezwW3To45UEh4TJCt1XYsGxd5VyjUnn1GujGE%2BIY1aSs8mL0MEIDryJT%2F5ue6gIrw4FcR%2BT2H6xTwghw7qghZ%2Bt9XpKhCEzcOz7Otu1%2BW4Ndp20%2FdgyrpPkwD%2BdEPGYqU%2FBA5J9PH%2F9cMyUqGcoJyTtTPfF5ZlqQnQcRnQqL6EFWJ0tlotUxpGr2zDt%2FjgM5P8xB0qhdgSyk2Kw5h3xLCXhqutKceFXCBLNM95trpPal%2BHkwJLLK1W30opbVlm7vqSQMuTZ%2FKqBh9uFpQlQaewWTQemmN4Zy9QFx%2B8cn%2Btxzt0cYQSAEVI2Ea0J5WaV2M6AZ0Fmql%2B0eC5xoVduxNKWmGLtVgyGcKhMM7lQWacrsiaFlJkcaOkDqlzfPVhnwXQ4V5F3KDrOdI7PC%2Fks47S7%2F7TZIf9KTYNFs%2FwpmuLHrJxEd2RjmrEn7zzjROhLwZCxRqY8T0eKEKDLcmRUuLiqgBRDO%2BAVbyL99nSV1%2BHM1igGLAvwxJRWgdp0oc9KSOIl40zGyRM%2Bhf5l7Jlw2IlsEaWCL4it%2FVd0NzOkTO3F6LaRlFXTnR3f0UhidmItzCGZ0FBGoGC11MKHO98kGOqUBZe7Ra8aEETQ%2FAZQ070kukQpxQdurJ0jgkJXNKIoywwsylHDBp%2FxUn1P1C%2FGaeI1B8yEAG%2B7PSJmF1lh5uQd6VS%2FosFSvpRKbnxSYlzW182u37zsjN81U8l5hak4tiqUF3OxqQLZkzUB%2Bu6KOF0mVj2co%2FqdAy%2F%2FlWmSOJ%2BjIhttOSYjlJEU1nAalu%2FaB%2FUKjqQ%2FZAb3Dwaf3Z6Bg57eeA%2BSp8DXq&X-Amz-Signature=9d5eea1956256d0eb718e8eb2fd780523e0ba7ce2b352bb648cb317c979cbb7c&X-Amz-SignedHeaders=host&x-amz-checksum-mode=ENABLED&x-id=GetObject)
- We can now start filtering our data table and select only one specific student, for example the student Clotilde Runkle
```sql
SELECT *
FROM grades
INNER JOIN enrollments 
	ON enrollments.id = grades.enrollment_id
INNER JOIN courses 
	ON courses.id = enrollments.course_id
INNER JOIN students 
  ON students.id = enrollments.student_id
WHERE
	students.first_name = 'Clotilde'
	AND
	students.last_name = 'Runkle'

```

- Lastly, we can group or table by the different values in column `category` we must now also define how the numeric values should be aggregated, thus we specify AVG(grade) so that for each course category the average of the values in column `grade` is calculated
```sql
SELECT
	category, AVG(grade)
FROM grades
INNER JOIN enrollments 
	ON enrollments.id = grades.enrollment_id
INNER JOIN courses 
	ON courses.id = enrollments.course_id
INNER JOIN students 
  ON students.id = enrollments.student_id
WHERE
	students.first_name = 'Clotilde'
	AND
	students.last_name = 'Runkle'
GROUP BY category
```

- `MAX(grade)` â†’ 5.75
- `COUNT(grade)` â†’ 5
- 5.75 - 5 + 1.25 = 2

Our formula has following components:
- `z` is the salary of the current record we are in
- average(x) â†’ `AVG(salary)`
- max(x) â†’ `MAX(salary)`
- min(x) â†’ `MIN(salary)`
Thus, we can calculate:
`(salary - AVG(salary)) / MAX(salary) - MIN(salary)`

- Correct, we can also create a DataFrame from a numpy array or a dictionary.
- Incorrect, because the first answer is correct
- Incorrect, `pd.Series` are not the same. a `pd.Series` is usually represented by a single row or column in a DataFrame
- Incorrect, in a DataFrame we can also have a non-numeric index such as the name of Football players

[`pd.Series.argmax`](https://pandas.pydata.org/docs/reference/api/pandas.Series.argmax.html) â†’ returns the index position of the largest value in the Series
[`pd.Series.sum()`](https://pandas.pydata.org/docs/reference/api/pandas.Series.sum.html) â†’ returns the sum over all elements in the series

- Which is our `argmax`? â†’ Largest value? â†’ 42.0 â†’ Index position? â†’ <u>6</u>
- Which is our `sum`? â†’ 5.0 + 11.0 + 21.0 + 34.0 + 42.0 = <u>113</u>
- 6 + 113 = **119**

- Correct, with `df.iloc[0]` we access the first row which contains only 1â€™s
- Incorrect, with `df.loc['v']` we cannot access the column `v` but only the row with index-label `v`, however, there is no such row
- Correct, with `df.loc[:, ['v']]` we receive back a DataFrame and in this DataFrame we need to select the column `v` again which we do with `[â€™vâ€™]` and this gives us a Series
- Incorrect, with `df.a` we look for a column named `a`, however, there is none
- Correct, with `df.v` we access the column `v` which contains only 1â€™s
- Correct, with `df.loc['a']` we access the row `a` which contains only 1â€™s
- Incorrect, this does not give us back a Series but rather a DataFrame
- Incorrect, when using `.iloc[]` we cannot combine index positions (0) with labels (v)

- Incorrect, with [`pd.merge`](https://pandas.pydata.org/docs/reference/api/pandas.DataFrame.merge.html) we combine two DataFrames together
- Incorrect, with [`pd.reshape`](https://pandas.pydata.org/docs/user_guide/reshaping.html) we change the dimensions of a DataFrame
- Correct, this is exactly what the [`pd.melt`](https://pandas.pydata.org/docs/reference/api/pandas.melt.html) is doing, transforming a DataFrame from wide to long format
- Incorrect, with [`pd.pivot`](https://pandas.pydata.org/docs/reference/api/pandas.DataFrame.pivot.html) we create a pivot table to get more insights into data

We see that in this pivot table
- values in column `course` are the column names.
- values in column `region` are the index
- values in column `bachelor/master` are the values

Now we can answer the question:
- Incorrect, we use merge to combine two DataFrames and not to aggregate data
- Correct, because we are using merge but are aiming to pivot the DataFrame
- Incorrect, as we see in the desired output above, we see that `columns=` is set correctly, but `values=` is set incorrectly. However, we should not change the `columns=` parameter.
- Incorrect, of course we can do thinks like melt or pivot
- Correct, see in the desired output above, `region` should be the index and `bachelor/master `the values
- Correct, this is a pivot case

Letâ€™s look at one specific purchase in more detail:
```python
json.loads(ORDERS['products'][3]) # -> convert JSON string in line 3 to a dictionary

{
	'banana': 1,
	'book': 3,
	'car': 1,
	'chair': 1,
	'door': 1,
	'lamp': 1,
	'robot': 1,
	'smartphone': 2,
	'wallet': 1
}
```
We see that in the column `products` we have the information stored about how many items of each product were bought. 
For each purchase (record in the DataFrame), we want to know now how many items were bought on average per product type.
In our example we have 9 different products and 12 items in total. Thus, on average `12 / 9 = 1.33` items were bought. 
How can we compute this now using Python?
To get the sum of product items in the purchase we can execute:
```python
ORDERS.loc[3, 'products'].values()
[3, 1, 2, 1, 1, 1, 1, 1, 1] # -> all values in the dictionary

sum(ORDERS.loc[3, 'products'].values())
12 # -> sum of products bought
```
To get the number of different products in the purchase we can execute:
```python
ORDERS.loc[3, 'products'].keys()
['book', 'lamp', 'smartphone', 'door', 'car', 'banana', 'chair', 'robot', 'wallet'] # -> names of all the different products bought

len(ORDERS.loc[3, 'products'].keys())
9 # -> number of different products bought
```
We can combine it all:
```python
sum(ORDERS.loc[3, 'products'].values()) / len(ORDERS.loc[3, 'products'].keys())
1.3333333333333333 # -> average number of items bought per product type in purchase
```
And finally to execute the calculation above on the entire DataFrame, i.e., for each purchase we can make use of the `.apply()` function: 
```python
df['products'].apply(lambda r : sum(r.values()) / len(r.keys()))
```

- Correct, if we have integers (0, 1, 2, 3 etc.) stored in our index column, then this works
- Correct, if a column has the name 0
- Correct, we can access the first record with this command
- Incorrect, we can only provide integers as parameters to the `.iloc[]` selector

- Correct, we can first group per recipient and then aggregate the values of each recipient with `max` parameter, which yields the highest value for each column per recipient
- Correct, the `.max()` function returns the highest value
- Incorrect, `axis = 2` is not a valid parameter of the `.agg()` function
- Correct, we can also use `np.max` as parameter instead of `'max'`
- Incorrect, this gives us back the name of the recipient that comes last in the alphabet
- Incorrect, this gives us back the highest value in each of the three columns, but no name of a recipient

- We deal with a classification problem â†’ category
- We have a flower and three possible classes, our classifier should classify the flower with one of the three classes
- We have labeled data â†’ we have the labels y available, i.e., for each flower in the training set we know to which class it belongs to
- We have less than < 100k samples
- We can use a `LinearSVC`

We divide our data in k-folds and perform k train / test runs.

TP â†’ all samples classified as Setosa that in reality are Setosa
TP = 19 = 19
FP â†’ all samples classified as Setosa that in reality are not Setosa
FP = 6 + 6 = 12

Precision = 19 / (19 + 12) = 19 / 27 = 0.67

- Incorrect 
- Correct, when doing the `train_test_split()`, the data is split randomly by scikit-learn. Thus, the training and test data can differ on the next day which may lead to better or worse performance.
- Incorrect, k-Nearest-Neighbor always calculate the distances of a new sample to all other samples in the training set.
- Incorrect, the report is created based on the performance of the classifier on the test dataset

---

![image](https://prod-files-secure.s3.us-west-2.amazonaws.com/85904fa9-813f-4181-815c-7a9adaee3156/68a14e63-64a8-4e74-89a2-d81fd3bbd32f/Untitled.png?X-Amz-Algorithm=AWS4-HMAC-SHA256&X-Amz-Content-Sha256=UNSIGNED-PAYLOAD&X-Amz-Credential=ASIAZI2LB466YLHOPM7B%2F20251214%2Fus-west-2%2Fs3%2Faws4_request&X-Amz-Date=20251214T005142Z&X-Amz-Expires=3600&X-Amz-Security-Token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEF8aCXVzLXdlc3QtMiJIMEYCIQCBuISMaem2j5fjO6ysX4RqCdEBlYypMu9gtpncRVUUJQIhAKjXepEWFwhYiY0IejrUnooTDkPzEpNcNXrMEpVzTmwmKv8DCCcQABoMNjM3NDIzMTgzODA1IgwCoFxpATez995%2F2JEq3AM4izWMzUiYI%2F0k58mUWLkYqDN9buf8iHAsrhAij5LtMK7qA555OK6FEYdODjzw1v3SF2sqKYEQx1yIUU3NTCsdDXesftvtN7ll5Na7FRl1leQmW0NToqbBSQHeVoQhnxdNwSBQaI00xR0QrKybFcQKLnW%2FS6s2L8g9woslyVT0AD3o6eIKDtPZvIFFV%2FFdh1drdPIE3MStAXQjHkSH7leq9DUyh5RoqhIwIbsG9C26gqwv5INg0veTQ8xgKNRoQhQM5%2FCBdMV3egK80k02n4k3eKQwD%2BLRn6kAssptKrK%2Fpace9cUTGsh44e%2FueNWq%2Bo5uzTR5ARb2dE2ZtlJ4eE7kVLIqd8iBcOKBbHMaCrHt%2BBfFyW307eJqbOeoVt3waHqJ6IsFpEIDPi66FrShcqdkDgPBYz050ikBjiWrQ6TnvWd9ootp28mT42I9YJtekatIk7jRFCuxDrod5Fq0zg%2BHoSahCm9anMYMCmXM8X3fzHGiAAxwrAkH%2FZF8%2Fjg6THlQOlARzgmKi75IVlxUvQm49r9m1%2B72mbnwql6TodYkBs54IMOtNkeetcf6uxXGbVKlsGo1PzTtRPIAeqtTnnm42K1vCr%2Fdv1m%2FNyA4kCfmlrkRY1f32jJXRZAPKzCFzvfJBjqkAdfp9o%2FxpPh8Ho%2F%2FxRXYOcGEMZ2nsa8mYZYddEIxNQTr4T%2FhX7EbEPJY7MotFKMZWzHtXrccGWrvRYIAF%2FC3prAzEORfWR%2FEVnc8%2FZqL31sTWx33%2B65LvL7GQm54z%2Br9FxG7nfczGERQ4v383MBpxERuU%2F%2F2uxQlI%2BLiolvgJujlSX98IAr4QAyIJAw9RHa1GGnEuov2I7W6Hv37ecxWnpn1bT5q&X-Amz-Signature=12bc4a4ec593a3485b163c224ef0b105c5dceaa61a50bf8b24eb4d7ffa93a25d&X-Amz-SignedHeaders=host&x-amz-checksum-mode=ENABLED&x-id=GetObject)
- How many distances do we need to calculate for a new sample that we want to classify?
- We need to calculate the distance of this specific sample to all other samples
- How many other samples are there? 5948 samples
â†’ We need to calculate 5948 euclidean distances
- How long does it take to calculate one euclidean distance?
â†’ It takes 0.01 seconds to calculate one euclidean distance
- How long does it take to calculate 5948 euclidean distances and thus classify a sample?
â†’ It takes 5948 * 0.01 = 59.48 seconds
- How many samples can we classify in 15 hours?
- 15 hours are 15 * 3600 = 54â€™000 seconds
